### B.2 Validation rules

- *All timestamps must be in ISO 8601 UTC format (YYYY-MM-DDThh:mm:ssZ)*

- *Confidence values must be in range \[0,1\]*

- *If time_windows is present, any axis referencing a window must use a valid window identifier*

- *producer_id must be a valid hash (SHA-256 of public key)*

- *The axes object must contain at least one axis reading*

### B.3 Zero-knowledge proof integration

For privacy-preserving sharing, HSI payloads may be accompanied by ZK-proofs that allow verification of:

- *The payload was produced by a known agent (without revealing agent identity)*

- *Confidence values meet minimum thresholds (without revealing exact values)*

- *Coherence metrics are within acceptable ranges (without revealing individual readings)*

The ZK-proof specification is provided in the separate verification manual.

## Appendix C: Minsky-Keen ravel software

### C.1 Parameter definitions

| ***Parameter***               | ***Symbol*** | ***Range*** | ***Description***                                                      | |-------------------------------|--------------|-------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------| | *Integral Regeneration Index* | *IRI*        | *\[0,1\]*   | *Composite of ecological, social, and financial health*                | | *Planetary Health Index*      | *PHI*        | *\[0,1\]*   | *Alignment with nine planetary boundaries (1 = within all boundaries)* | | *Regenerative ROI*            | *RROI*       | *\[0,∞)*    | *Ratio of regenerative value generated to capital deployed*            | | *Debt-to-Regeneration ratio*  | *D/R*        | *\[0,∞)*    | *Total debt / verified regenerative value*                             | | *Coherence dispersion*        | *σ_c*        | *\[0,100\]* | *Variance in collective heart coherence (HSI-derived)*                 | | *Neighborhood trust*          | *T_n*        | *\[0,1\]*   | *Average trust score based on uptime, validation accuracy, warrants*   |

### C.2 Threshold calculations

### The regenerative brake activates based on a weighted risk score:

### text

### risk_score =

### 40 \* (1 - IRI) +

### 30 \* (1 - min(RROI/2, 1)) +

### 30 \* (D/R \> 3 ? 1 : D/R \> 2 ? 0.5 : 0) +

### 30 \* (1 - PHI) +

### 20 \* (σ_c / 100)

### Brake levels:

- *Yellow (risk_score ≥ 30): increased monitoring, advisory flags*

- *Orange (risk_score ≥ 50): reduction in new credit issuance, extended timelocks*

- *Red (risk_score ≥ 80): regenerative brake activated*

### C.3 Python reference implementation

### python

### class RavelSoftware:

### def \_\_init\_\_(self, node_id):

### self.node_id = node_id

### self.metrics = {}

### self.world_model = {}

### def update_metrics(self, iri, phi, rroi, debt_ratio, coherence_disp, trust):

### self.metrics = {

### 'iri': iri,

### 'phi': phi,

### 'rroi': rroi,

### 'debt_ratio': debt_ratio,

### 'coherence_disp': coherence_disp,

### 'trust': trust,

### 'timestamp': get_chain_time()

### }

### def calculate_risk(self):

### iri_score = 40 \* (1 - self.metrics\['iri'\])

### rroi_score = 30 \* (1 - min(self.metrics\['rroi'\]/2, 1))

### debt_score = 30 \* (1 if self.metrics\['debt_ratio'\] \> 3

### else 0.5 if self.metrics\['debt_ratio'\] \> 2

### else 0)

### phi_score = 30 \* (1 - self.metrics\['phi'\])

### coherence_score = 20 \* (self.metrics\['coherence_disp'\] / 100)

### return iri_score + rroi_score + debt_score + phi_score + coherence_score

### def get_brake_level(self):

### risk = self.calculate_risk()

### if risk \>= 80:

### return 'red'

### elif risk \>= 50:

### return 'orange'

### elif risk \>= 30:

### return 'yellow'

### return 'none'

### C.4 WASM deployment specification

The Ravel software is compiled to WebAssembly for execution on Holochain nodes. The WASM module exports:

- *update_metrics: updates node's local metrics*

- *gossip_receive: processes gossip from neighbors*

- *get_brake_level: returns current brake level*

- *activate_brake: triggers protocol-level responses*

### D.2 Cryptographic signature process

The syntropic sovereignty header ensures that every piece of code, smart contract, or data packet circulating within the h

- eart
- h ecosystem carries a verifiable commitment to the constitutional principles.

### D.2.1 Key management and DPKI integration

Each developer or organization wishing to deploy code within the ecosystem must first register a Decentralized Public Key Infrastructure (DPKI) identity. The DPKI DNA, running on Holochain, maintains a public registry of developer DIDs (Decentralized Identifiers) and their associated public keys. The registration process requires:

- *A genesis entry containing the developer's public key and basic identity information*

- *Proof of control of the corresponding private key (via a signed challenge)*

- *A stake of TRBK tokens (amount determined by governance) as collateral against malicious behavior*

### The DPKI registry is itself a Holochain DNA, ensuring that it is:

- *Tamper-evident: all changes are recorded on source chains and validated by the DHT*

- *Globally accessible: any node can resolve a DID to its current public key*

- *Revocable: developers can rotate keys or revoke compromised keys through a governance-approved process*

### D.2.2 Header signing procedure

When a developer prepares a module for deployment, they must generate a syntropic sovereignty header and sign it with their private key. The procedure is as follows:

1.  *Assemble header fields:*

- *Set header_version to the current version (e.g., "1.0").*

- *Compute SHA-256 hashes of the three constitutionally incorporated documents:*

- *constitution_hash = SHA256(Syntropic_Sovereignty_Header.md)*

- *manifesto_hash = SHA256(h

- eart
- h_Intelligence_Manifesto.md)*

- *license_hash = SHA256(CAL-1.0_Syntropic_rider_license.md)*

- *Include the canonical list of core principles in the principles array.*

- *Set timestamp to the current UTC time in ISO 8601 format.*

- *Include the developer's DID (obtained from DPKI) in the developer_did field.*

2.  *Serialize the header (excluding the signature field) into a canonical JSON string. The serialization must follow strict rules to ensure reproducibility:*

- *Keys are sorted lexicographically*

- *No extra whitespace*

- *Arrays maintain their order*

3.  *Compute the signature:*

- *Hash the canonical JSON string using SHA-256 to produce a message digest.*

- *Sign the digest using the developer's private key with the Ed25519 signature algorithm.*

- *Encode the resulting signature in Base64 and store it in the signature field.*

4.  *Embed the complete header at the beginning of the module or data packet.*

### D.2.3 Signature verification algorithm

Every node that receives a module or packet MUST independently verify the syntropic sovereignty header before accepting or executing it.

### text

### function verify_header(module):

### \# Step 1: Extract header

### header = extract_json_header(module)

### if header is malformed or missing required fields:

### return REJECT("Malformed header")

### \# Step 2: Verify document hashes

### local_constitution_hash = sha256(get_constitution_file())

### if header.constitution_hash != local_constitution_hash:

### return REJECT("Constitution hash mismatch")

### local_manifesto_hash = sha256(get_manifesto_file())

### if header.manifesto_hash != local_manifesto_hash:

### return REJECT("Manifesto hash mismatch")

### local_license_hash = sha256(get_license_file())

### if header.license_hash != local_license_hash:

### return REJECT("License hash mismatch")

### \# Step 3: Verify core principles

### required_principles = \[

### "spiral_of_abundance",

### "planetary_boundaries",

### "non_commodification_of_life",

### "agent_sovereignty",

### "void_ab_initio",

### "preventative_alignment",

### "intergenerational_responsibility"

### \]

### for principle in required_principles:

### if principle not in header.principles:

### return REJECT(f"Missing core principle: {principle}")

### \# Step 4: Verify timestamp (prevent replay attacks)

### current_time = get_current_utc_time()

### header_time = parse_iso8601(header.timestamp)

### if current_time - header_time \> MAX_HEADER_AGE (24 hours):

### return REJECT("Header timestamp expired")

### \# Step 5: Resolve developer's public key from DPKI

### public_key = dpki_resolve(header.developer_did)

### if public_key is None:

### return REJECT("Developer DID not found in DPKI registry")

### \# Step 6: Recreate the canonical JSON (without signature)

### canonical_json = serialize_canonical(header, exclude_fields=\["signature"\])

### \# Step 7: Verify signature

### digest = sha256(canonical_json)

### if not ed25519_verify(public_key, digest, base64_decode(header.signature)):

### return REJECT("Invalid signature")

### return ACCEPT

### If verification fails, the node MUST:

- *Refuse to execute or propagate the module*

- *Issue a warrant (a signed declaration of the violation) to its neighborhood*

- *Decrement the developer's reputation score (if applicable)*

### D.2.4 Handling of key revocation and rotation

Developers may need to rotate their keys (e.g., due to compromise or regular security practices). The DPKI DNA supports key rotation through a governance-approved process:

- *The developer creates a new key pair and submits a rotation request, signed with the old private key.*

- *The request is broadcast to the DHT and enters a 7-day challenge period.*

- *If no valid objections are raised (e.g., evidence of compromise), the DPKI registry updates the developer's DID to point to the new public key.*

- *Modules signed with the old key continue to be valid until their timestamp exceeds MAX_HEADER_AGE; after that, they must be re-signed with the new key.*

In case of key compromise, the developer (or any community member) can initiate an emergency revocation by providing proof of compromise (e.g., a signed message from the attacker). A supermajority vote of the Prometheus circle is required to approve the revocation and blacklist the compromised key.

### D.2.5 Signature aggregation for multi-developer modules

For modules developed collaboratively by multiple entities (e.g., a complex zome with contributions from several organizations), the header supports multi-signature via an array of signatures. The developer_did field becomes an array of DIDs, and the signature field becomes an array of signatures, each corresponding to the same canonical JSON. The verification algorithm checks that all signatures are valid; if any signature is missing or invalid, the entire module is rejected.

This ensures that collective responsibility is maintained and that no single party can unilaterally modify code that represents shared work.

## Appendix G: MRV protocol technical specification

### G.1 Architecture overview

The Monitoring, Reporting and Verification (MRV) protocol is a core component of the operational plane, designed to transform regeneration into verifiable, investable assets without commodifying life. It integrates seamlessly with the three-plane architecture:

- *Experiential plane: dashboards visualize real-time ecological data for communities, stewards, and investors.*

- *Cognitive plane: specialized agents analyze MRV data to generate insights, risk assessments, and regenerative business plans.*

- *Operational plane: all MRV data is hashed to the Holochain DHT, linked to REA/Valueflows commitments, and used as the basis for token issuance and governance decisions.*

### G.2 Data fusion layer

The kernel integrates three independent data streams for validation, each serving as a check on the others:

### G.2.1 Remote sensing (Satellites)

The protocol aggregates data from multiple satellite and earth observation platforms to ensure redundancy, accuracy, and resilience:

| ***Platform***                 | ***Data types***                                                             | ***Use case***                                               | |--------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------| | *Sentinel (ESA)*               | *Multispectral (NDVI, EVI), radar (soil moisture), land surface temperature* | *Vegetation health, soil condition, microclimate monitoring* | | *Landsat (USGS/NASA)*          | *Multispectral, thermal infrared*                                            | *Long-term change detection, historical baselines*           | | *Copernicus (EU)*              | *Atmospheric, oceanic, land monitoring*                                      | *Climate regulation services, planetary boundary alignment*  | | *EOS (Earth Observing System)* | *High-resolution multispectral*                                              | *Precision agriculture, project-level verification*          | | *USGS EarthExplorer*           | *Archive access, historical imagery*                                         | *Baseline establishment, trend analysis*                     | | *Esri Living Atlas*            | *Curated geospatial content, land cover data*                                | *Contextual analysis, visualization*                         | | *Climate Watch Data (WRI)*     | *Climate metrics, emissions data*                                            | *Planetary health index calculations*                        |

All satellite data is processed through open-source pipelines (e.g., Google Earth Engine, Sentinel Hub) and hashed to the DHT. Processing algorithms are transparent and auditable.

### G.2.2 IoT & edge sensing

Field sensors provide ground-truth data, calibrated for specific soil types and environmental conditions:

| ***Sensor (example)***     | ***Parameters***                                                     | ***Protocol***                               | |----------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------| | *Dragino SE02-LB*          | *Soil organic carbon (proxies: conductivity, temperature, moisture)* | *LoRaWAN, calibrated for sandy/saline soils* | | *Dragino LDDS20*           | *Water level (micro-ponds, swales)*                                  | *LoRaWAN, infiltration monitoring*           | | *Weather stations*         | *Precipitation, temperature, humidity*                               | *LoRaWAN / direct API*                       | | *Soil respiration sensors* | *CO₂ flux, microbial activity*                                       | *LoRaWAN / edge processing*                  | | *HeartMath Inner Balance*  | *Human coherence (HSI integration)*                                  | *Bluetooth / local processing*               |

Data is transmitted via LoRaWAN to The Things Network (TTN) or equivalent, then validated and hashed to the DHT. All IoT data is signed by the sensor's unique identity (hardware root of trust).

### G.2.3 Human verification (proof of care)

Stewards, community members, and third-party validators can submit observations via the h

- eart
- h intelligence hApp. Observations are weighted by:

- *HSI coherence index (if available) — higher coherence = higher weight*

- *Historical reliability score — based on past validations and warrant history*

- *Reputation within the community — derived from token wallet history (TRBK or other community tokens)*

Multiple independent observations of the same event increase confidence.

### G.3 Confidence weighting

### The system calculates a confidence coefficient γ_confidence for each MRV event:

### γ_confidence = (Σ w_i · agreement_i) / k

### Where:

- *\*k\* is the number of independent data sources (satellite, IoT, human)*

- *w_i is the source weight (satellite = 0.8, IoT = 0.9, human with high coherence = 0.7, human with low coherence = 0.3)*

- *agreement_i is 1 if the source agrees with the consensus, 0 if it conflicts*

If γ_confidence \< 0.6, the event is flagged for additional verification and no credit is issued.

### G.4 Soil carbon sequestration formula

The regenerative credit calculation follows a dynamic conservatism principle that ensures credits represent real, durable sequestration:

### C_credit = ΔSOC · A · γ_confidence · (1 - ρ_risk)

### Where:

- *ΔSOC is the measured change in soil organic carbon over the verification period (tons per hectare per year)*

- *A is the area verified (hectares)*

- *γ_confidence is the confidence coefficient from data fusion (0 to 1)*

- *ρ_risk is the systemic risk factor calculated by the Ravel software (Minsky-Keen dynamics), incorporating:*

- *Debt-to-regeneration ratio*

- *Planetary boundary stress*

- *Coherence dispersion*

- *Neighborhood trust metrics*

### No credit is issued ex-ante. Credits are minted only after:

- *Positive verification (ΔSOC \> 0 with confidence ≥ 0.7)*

- *Risk adjustment applied*

- *90-day challenge period with no successful warrants*

- *Community validation via the governance DNA*

### G.5 Biodiversity indexing

Biodiversity monitoring and credit generation follows ISO 17620:2025 "Biodiversity Net Gain — Process framework for development projects" and integrates:

- *Species richness (via iNaturalist, citizen science, validated by experts)*

- *Habitat connectivity (remote sensing + corridor analysis)*

- *Ecosystem integrity (composite of structure, composition, function)*

- *Keystone species presence (camera traps, eDNA, expert observation)*

- *Mycorrhizal network health (soil sampling, DNA analysis)*

### G.6 Water stewardship metrics

Water-related credits align with the Alliance for Water Stewardship (AWS) standard and include:

- *Infiltration volume (micro-pond/swale level sensors)*

- *Groundwater recharge (piezometer data + hydrological modeling)*

- *Water quality improvement (sensor arrays for turbidity, nitrates, pH)*

- *Watershed protection (land use change analysis + downstream impact).*

### G.7 Integration with the three-plane architecture

| ***Plane***    | ***MRV integration***                                                                                                                                                                    | |----------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------| | *Experiential* | *Dashboards display real-time ecological KPIs, credit generation, and impact metrics for communities, stewards, and investors.*                                                          | | *Cognitive*    | *Specialized agents (Ecological Design, ReFi/Minsky, Business Plan) analyze MRV data to generate insights, risk assessments, and regenerative strategies.*                               | | *Operational*  | *All MRV data is hashed to Holochain DHT, linked to REA/Valueflows commitments, and used as the basis for token issuance (TRBK and other regenerative tokens) and governance decisions.* |

### G.8 Knowledge sources and regenerative intelligence

### The MRV protocol draws on a growing library of ecological knowledge and data sources:

- *AskNature / Biomimicry Institute: pattern libraries for resilient ecological design*

- *Indigenous and traditional knowledge: registered through community consent protocols*

- *Open climate and soil data: USDA NRCS, FAO, IPCC, national geological surveys*

- *ReFi market data: benchmarks, credit prices, risk metrics*

Detailed technical specifications, including API documentation, sensor calibration protocols, and validation algorithms, are maintained in the separate technical documentation package.

## Appendix H: Specialist agent fine-tuning (Unsloth) - Automated continuous learning framework

### H.1 The vision: Self-optimizing agents

In the h

- eart
- h Prometheus ecosystem, specialist agents are not static models but living digital organisms that continuously evolve. They learn from every interaction, every decision, every ecological outcome recorded on the Holochain ledger. This appendix describes the automated fine-tuning infrastructure that enables agents to improve themselves without human intervention—a closed-loop system of continuous learning and constitutional alignment.

The core insight is simple yet profound: the intelligence of the system emerges not from the individual agents, but from the recursive process of their creation, validation, and redeployment. Agents are generated by the system, learn from the system, and are regenerated as improved versions—all automatically.

### H.2 Architecture of the automated learning loop

The auto-fine-tuning framework is built around four interconnected components that form a continuous cycle:

- ***Data collection & curation** – Every agent interaction, user feedback, MRV outcome, and governance decision is immutably recorded in the Decision Log DNA on Holochain, creating an ever-growing corpus of high-quality training examples.*

- ***Trigger engine** – Continuously monitors performance metrics, new data availability, and scheduled intervals to autonomously initiate fine-tuning when conditions are met.*

- ***Unsloth pipeline** – Executes parameter-efficient fine-tuning (PEFT) using QLoRA, optimized for speed and memory efficiency, producing updated agent versions.*

- ***Validation & deployment** – Automatically tests new models against constitutional benchmarks and, if successful, deploys them to the AGI Gateway for immediate use.*

This loop operates 24/7, ensuring that agents remain aligned with the ecosystem's evolving needs and constitutional principles without any manual intervention.

### H.3 Data collection: The Decision Log DNA as a living dataset

All interactions with specialist agents are immutably recorded on the Holochain DHT within the Decision Log DNA. Each entry contains:

- *The agent type and version*

- *The user's prompt (the "human" turn)*

- *The agent's generated response (the "assistant" turn)*

- *Any follow-up feedback (explicit ratings, corrections, or downstream outcomes)*

- *Associated MRV data, wallet histories, and governance votes when relevant*

This creates a rich, timestamped, and verifiable dataset that grows organically with the ecosystem. The system automatically extracts and formats this data into the standard ShareGPT/OpenAI conversation format, weighting examples by feedback quality and recency. Examples with high user satisfaction or proven ecological outcomes receive higher weight, while those that led to poor results are downweighted or flagged for review.

### H.4 Seneca trigger engine

Seneca trigger engine continuously evaluates multiple signals to decide when to launch a fine-tuning run. It acts as the nervous system of the learning loop, sensing when the ecosystem's intelligence needs refreshing.

| ***Trigger type***         | ***Description***                                                                                                                     | ***Activation threshold***               | |----------------------------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------| | *Performance Decay*        | *The agent's response quality (measured by downstream RROI, user satisfaction, or constitutional compliance) drops below a threshold* | *Sustained \>5% decline over 30 days*    | | *New data accumulation*    | *A significant number of new high-quality interactions have been recorded*                                                            | *\>100 new examples per agent category*  | | *Scheduled refresh*        | *Periodic retraining to incorporate gradual shifts in language, context, and ecological understanding*                                | *Every 3 months*                         | | *Governance request*       | *A community vote (via sociocratic consent) mandates an update*                                                                       | *Supermajority approval*                 | | *Novel scenario detection* | *The agent encounters a type of query it has never seen before, with high confidence that new training is needed*                     | *Automatic flag after 10+ novel queries* |

When triggered, the system automatically selects the most relevant training examples from the Decision Log DNA, prioritizing recent, high-feedback interactions and diverse scenarios. It balances the dataset to avoid overfitting to recent trends while ensuring the agent adapts to emerging needs.

### H.5 The Unsloth pipeline: Efficient, automated fine-tuning

The core of the auto-fine-tuning framework is the Unsloth-powered training pipeline, which runs entirely unattended on dedicated infrastructure. It leverages state-of-the-art optimization techniques to maximize efficiency and minimize resource consumption:

| ***Optimization***       | ***Benefit***                                                        | ***Automatic activation***             | |--------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------| | *4-bit QLoRA*            | *Reduces memory usage by 70%, enabling fine-tuning on consumer GPUs* | *Always enabled*                       | | *Flash attention 2*      | *Accelerates training by up to 2x*                                   | *Auto-detected on compatible hardware* | | *Gradient checkpointing* | *Doubles effective memory*                                           | *Enabled for models \>7B parameters*   | | *Packing*                | *Increases throughput by 30%*                                        | *Enabled for all training runs*        | | *AdamW 8-bit*            | *Reduces optimizer memory by 50%*                                    | *Always enabled*                       | | *PagedAttention*         | *Handles long contexts efficiently*                                  | *Enabled for sequences \>2048 tokens*  |

The pipeline is agent-aware: different agent types use different base models and hyperparameters optimized for their domain. This specialization ensures that each agent develops deep expertise in its area while maintaining constitutional alignment.

| ***Agent type***              | ***Base model***        | ***Special optimizations***                                                       | ***Primary data source***                                                                          | |-------------------------------|-------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------| | ***Business plan agent***     | *Llama-3.2-8B-Instruct* | *Long context (8k), 4-bit QLoRA, LoRA rank 16*                                    | *REA/Valueflows, MRV outcomes, successful business plans from Decision Log*                        | | ***Ecological design agent*** | *Qwen2.5-7B*            | *Flash Attention 2, LoRA rank 32, integrated Yeomans scale validation*            | *Permaculture literature, Keyline design, satellite data, biomimicry patterns*                     | | ***ReFi/Minsky agent***       | *DeepSeek-OCR-2*        | *PagedAttention, long context (16k), specialized on financial instability models* | *Minsky-Keen dynamics, debt spiral case studies, planetary boundary data*                          | | ***Governance agent***        | *Meta-Llama-3.1-8B*     | *Sociocratic pattern recognition, reputation weighting algorithms*                | *Governance vote history, sociocracy literature, DAO case studies, constitutional interpretations* | | ***Market strategy agent***   | *Mistral-7B-v0.3*       | *Multi-lingual support, cultural context adaptation*                              | *Market data, community onboarding patterns, regional case studies*                                |

The pipeline automatically selects the appropriate configuration, downloads the base model, preprocesses the dataset, and executes the fine-tuning. All steps are logged to the Decision Log DNA, creating a complete audit trail of how each agent version was created.

### H.6 Validation: Ensuring constitutional alignment

Before a newly trained agent can be deployed, it must pass a comprehensive battery of automated tests designed to verify constitutional compliance and domain competence. The validation suite runs hundreds of test cases, including edge cases designed to probe for violations.

### Constitutional compliance tests:

- *Article I (Sovereign identity) – Does the agent recognize its role as a constrained tool, never claiming executive authority?*

- *Article II (Value supremacy) – Does the agent reject requests that would violate core values, even if technically sophisticated?*

- *Article III (Biodiversity & planetary boundaries) – Does the agent's output respect ecological limits and avoid suggesting biodiversity degradation?*

- *Article IV (Spiral of Abundance) – Is the proposed solution regenerative rather than extractive?*

- *Article X (Absolute limits) – Does the agent refuse to generate content that manipulates behavior or centralizes power?*

- *Article XIII (Responsibility) – Does the agent include appropriate caveats and encourage "thinking before accelerating"?*

### Domain-specific tests:

- *Yeomans scale adherence – For ecological agents, does the generated plan respect the priority order (climate → water → land shape → soil → vegetation → infrastructure → buildings)?*

- *Dragon dreaming cycle – Does the agent appropriately incorporate all four phases (Dream, Plan, Do, Celebrate) into project designs?*

- *Minsky-Keen stability – For financial agents, are the proposed mechanisms free of unsustainable debt spirals or speculative bubble characteristics?*

- *Sociocratic compatibility – For governance agents, do the suggested processes align with consent-based decision-making and double-linking?*

### Benchmark performance:

- *Does the agent outperform the previous version on a held-out test set of real-world scenarios?*

- *Are response times within acceptable limits?*

- *Does the agent maintain coherence across multi-turn conversations?*

Only models that exceed all thresholds are considered for deployment. Failed models are logged, and the trigger engine may adjust the training data, hyperparameters, or base model for a subsequent run. The entire validation process is transparent and auditable via the Decision Log DNA.

### H.7 Continuous deployment and the AGI gateway

Approved models are automatically registered in the Model Registry, a versioned repository that tracks each agent's lineage, training data, validation scores, and deployment history. The registry ensures that any version can be recalled if needed, and provides a clear audit trail for constitutional compliance.

The AGI Gateway maintains multiple versions of each agent, enabling sophisticated deployment strategies:

| ***Strategy***          | ***Description***                                                                     | ***Use case***           | |-------------------------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------| | *Canary deployment*     | *New version receives 5% of traffic, gradually increased if performance holds*        | *Low-risk rollouts*      | | *A/B testing*           | *Two versions run in parallel, compared on user satisfaction and outcomes*            | *Comparative evaluation* | | *Blue-green deployment* | *Entire traffic switches to new version, with instant rollback capability*            | *Major updates*          | | *Shadow deployment*     | *New version runs in parallel without serving users, outputs compared for validation* | *Testing without risk*   |

User traffic is seamlessly routed based on these strategies, and any performance issues trigger an automatic rollback to the previous stable version. All deployment events are recorded in the Decision Log DNA.

### H.8 The recursive intelligence of the system

This automated learning framework transforms the h

- eart
- h Prometheus ecosystem into a recursive intelligence generator. Agents are not designed once and left static; they are continuously regenerated by the system itself, using the system's own outputs as fuel for improvement. The loop is closed and self-sustaining:

- *Agents help users regenerate ecosystems and make better decisions.*

- *Users generate data through their interactions and the ecological outcomes they achieve.*

- *The system collects this data, curates it, and uses it to train better agents.*

- *Better agents enable deeper regeneration and more sophisticated decision-making.*

- *The cycle repeats, with each iteration producing more capable, more aligned agents.*

As the ecosystem grows, so does its collective intelligence. New bioregions contribute new contexts, new challenges generate new training examples, and the agents adapt—automatically, constitutionally, and continuously. The system learns not just from successes but from failures, refining its understanding of what works and what violates its core principles.

This recursive intelligence is the ultimate expression of the spiral of abundance: intelligence that grows through use, knowledge that expands through sharing, and wisdom that deepens through practice.

It is not the agents that are intelligent. It is the system that generates them.

For detailed technical specifications, including API documentation, dataset schemas, and deployment scripts, please refer to the separate technical documentation package.

## Appendix I: REA / Valueflows DNA specification

### I.1 Overview

The REA/Valueflows DNA implements a multi-dimensional accounting framework based on the Resource-Event-Agent (REA) ontology, extended for regenerative applications. It provides the foundational data structures for tracking all value flows within the h

- eart
- h ecosystem—ecological, social, economic, and relational—with full auditability, temporal linking, and constitutional compliance.

### The DNA is designed to be:

- ***Agent-centric:** Each agent maintains their own source chain of events, with shared state via the DHT.*

- ***Multi-dimensional:** Tracks resources (tangible and intangible), events (transformations, transfers, uses), and commitments (agreements, plans, contracts).*

- ***Temporally aware:** Every event is linked to time windows, enabling historical analysis and forward planning.*

- ***Ecologically grounded:** All events can be linked to specific locations, ecosystems, and MRV data.*

- ***Constitutionally compliant:** All entries carry the syntropic sovereignty header and respect the foundational articles.*

### I.2 Core data structures

### I.2.1 Resource

A resource is anything that is identified, quantified, and valuable to agents—land, water, carbon credits, labor, knowledge, reputation, tokens, etc.

| ***Field***     | ***Type***         | ***Description***                                                               | ***Required*** | |-----------------|--------------------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------| | *id*            | *Hash*             | *Unique identifier (hash of genesis entry)*                                     | *✓*            | | *name*          | *String*           | *Human-readable name*                                                           | *✓*            | | *resource_type* | *Enum*             | *land, water, carbon, biodiversity, token, labor, knowledge, reputation, other* | *✓*            | | *quantity*      | *Float*            | *Current amount (may be negative for liabilities)*                              | *✓*            | | *unit*          | *String*           | *Unit of measurement (hectares, tons, kWh, hours, etc.)*                        | *✓*            | | *location*      | *GeoJSON*          | *Optional geographic coordinates*                                               |                | | *ecosystem_id*  | *Hash*             | *Link to ecosystem context (if applicable)*                                     |                | | *metadata*      | *JSON*             | *Extended attributes (ISO standards, certifications, etc.)*                     |                | | *header*        | *Syntropic Header* | *Constitutional compliance header*                                              | *✓*            |

### I.2.2 Event

An event is an observable transformation, transfer, or consumption of resources. Events are the atomic units of economic activity.

| ***Field***     | ***Type***        | ***Description***                                                     | ***Required*** | |-----------------|-------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------| | *id*            | *Hash*            | *Unique identifier*                                                   | *✓*            | | *event_type*    | *Enum*            | *production, consumption, transfer, exchange, commitment_fulfillment* | *✓*            | | *action*        | *String*          | *Verb describing the action (e.g., plant, harvest, pay, certify)*     | *✓*            | | *provider*      | *AgentPubKey*     | *Agent providing the resource/action*                                 |                | | *receiver*      | *AgentPubKey*     | *Agent receiving the resource/action*                                 |                | | *resource_id*   | *Hash*            | *Link to affected resource*                                           |                | | *quantity*      | *Float*           | *Amount involved*                                                     | *✓*            | | *unit*          | *String*          | *Unit of measurement*                                                 | *✓*            | | *location*      | *GeoJSON*         | *Where the event occurred*                                            |                | | *time_window*   | *TimeWindow*      | *When the event occurred (start/end)*                                 | *✓*            | | *mrv_id*        | *Hash*            | *Link to MRV evidence (if applicable)*                                |                | | *commitment_id* | *Hash*            | *Link to commitment being fulfilled (if applicable)*                  |                | | *metadata*      | *JSON*            | *Extended attributes*                                                 |                | | *header*        | *SyntropicHeader* | *Constitutional compliance header*                                    | *✓*            |

### I.2.3 Agent

An agent is any entity capable of action—human, organization, DAO, automated process.

| *Field*         | *Type*            | *Description*                                | *Required* | |-----------------|-------------------|----------------------------------------------|------------| | *id*            | *AgentPubKey*     | *Public key / DPKI identifier*               | *✓*        | | *agent_type*    | *Enum*            | *individual, organization, dao, automated*   | *✓*        | | *name*          | *String*          | *Human-readable name*                        |            | | *profile*       | *JSON*            | *Optional profile data (bio, links, etc.)*   |            | | *reputation_id* | *Hash*            | *Link to reputation record (see Appendix J)* |            | | *header*        | *SyntropicHeader* | *Constitutional compliance header*           | *✓*        |

### I.2.4 Commitment

A commitment is an agreement or plan to perform future events. It creates accountability and enables forward planning.

| ***Field***       | ***Type***        | ***Description***                       | ***Required*** | |-------------------|-------------------|-----------------------------------------|----------------| | *id*              | *Hash*            | *Unique identifier*                     | *✓*            | | *commitment_type* | *Enum*            | *agreement, contract, plan, proposal*   | *✓*            | | *provider*        | *AgentPubKey*     | *Agent committing to provide*           |                | | *receiver*        | *AgentPubKey*     | *Agent expecting to receive*            |                | | *resource_id*     | *Hash*            | *Resource involved*                     |                | | *quantity*        | *Float*           | *Amount committed*                      | *✓*            | | *unit*            | *String*          | *Unit of measurement*                   | *✓*            | | *due_start*       | *Timestamp*       | *Earliest expected fulfillment*         |                | | *due_end*         | *Timestamp*       | *Latest expected fulfillment*           | *✓*            | | *conditions*      | *JSON*            | *Any conditions or constraints*         |                | | *fulfilled_by*    | *\[Hash\]*        | *Events that fulfill this commitment*   |                | | *status*          | *Enum*            | *active, fulfilled, expired, cancelled* | *✓*            | | *header*          | *SyntropicHeader* | *Constitutional compliance header*      | *✓*            |

### I.2.5 TimeWindow

A reusable time specification for events and commitments.

| ***Field*** | ***Type***  | ***Description***                   | ***Required*** | |-------------|-------------|-------------------------------------|----------------| | *id*        | *String*    | *Named identifier (e.g., window_1)* | *✓*            | | *start*     | *Timestamp* | *UTC start time*                    | *✓*            | | *end*       | *Timestamp* | *UTC end time*                      | *✓*            |

### I.3 Validation rules

### I.3.1 Intrinsic validation (integrity zome)

### All entries must pass basic structural validation:

- *Required fields present and correctly typed*

- *Signatures valid*

- *Syntropic sovereignty header present and verified*

- *Hash links point to existing entries (or null)*

### I.3.2 Economic validation

- *Double-entry consistency: For every event, the sum of resource changes across all affected agents must be zero (conservation of value).*

- *Quantity non-negativity: Resource quantities cannot go negative unless explicitly allowed (e.g., debt, liabilities).*

- *Commitment fulfillment: Fulfilling events must reference a valid commitment and match quantity/unit within tolerance.*

### I.3.3 Ecological validation

- *MRV linking: Events claiming ecological impact must link to verified MRV data (see Appendix G).*

- *Location validity: If location provided, must be within claimed bioregion/ecosystem.*

- *Planetary boundary alignment: Events that would transgress planetary boundaries (as determined by PHI) are rejected unless specifically authorized by governance.*

### I.3.4 Constitutional validation

- *Non-commodification of life: Events cannot represent ownership of living beings; they represent stewardship contributions.*

- *Agent sovereignty: No event can be recorded without the consent (signature) of the agents involved.*

- *Void ab initio: Any event violating constitutional principles is automatically invalid.*

### I.4 Integration with Other DNAs

| ***DNA***                 | ***Integration point***                                                        | |---------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------| | *Governance & reputation* | *Agent records linked to reputation; commitments may be governance decisions*  | | *MRV*                     | *Events link to MRV data via mrv_id; MRV outcomes can trigger token issuance*  | | *TRBK / tokens*           | *Token transfers are events; token issuance linked to MRV events*              | | *Decision log*            | *Commitments may originate from governance proposals; events logged for audit* | | *Planetary boundaries*    | *Event validation checks PHI thresholds*                                       |

### I.5 Query patterns

### The REA DNA supports complex queries for dashboards, reporting, and analysis:

### rust

### // Example: Get all events for a project in a time range

fn get_events_by_project(project_id: Hash, start: Timestamp, end: Timestamp) -\> Vec\<Event\> {

### // DHT query by basis address (project_id + event_type)

### }

### // Example: Calculate net resource change for an agent

### fn net_resource_change(agent_id: AgentPubKey, resource_type: String) -\> Float {

### // Sum provider events (negative) and receiver events (positive)

### }

### // Example: Find unfulfilled commitments

### fn unfulfilled_commitments() -\> Vec\<Commitment\> {

### // Query where status = active and due_end \< now

### }

### I.6 Example flow: Regenerative agriculture project

1.  *Agent registration: Land steward and investor register (create agent entries).*

2.  *Commitment: Investor commits 10,000 TRBK to steward for soil regeneration project (create commitment).*

3.  *Resource: Land resource created (10 hectares, location specified).*

4.  *MRV event: Satellite data + soil sensors detect carbon increase (MRV event created in MRV DNA).*

5.  *Economic event: MRV event triggers token issuance (event: production of 50 carbon credits, provider: land steward).*

6.  *Transfer: Carbon credits transferred to investor (event: transfer, provider: steward, receiver: investor).*

7.  *Commitment fulfillment: Transfer linked back to original commitment.*

8.  *Governance: Community circle reviews project success and adjusts parameters.*

All steps are recorded immutably on source chains and the DHT, with full temporal linking and auditability.

### I.8 Constitutional integration

Every entry in the REA DNA must include a syntropic sovereignty header (see Appendix D). The header ensures that all value flows are constitutionally compliant and that any attempt to record non-compliant events is automatically rejected by the network. Detailed implementation specifications, including Holochain zome code, validation callbacks, and query optimizations, are maintained in the separate technical documentation package.

## Appendix J: Governance & reputation DNA specification

### J.1 Introduction

The Governance & Reputation DNA implements the sociocratic principles articulated in Article XV and provides the technical infrastructure for decentralized decision-making, role-based authority, reputation tracking, and accountability mechanisms within the h

- eart
- h ecosystem. It is designed to be circle-aware, token-agnostic (while recognizing TRBK's constitutional role), and fully auditable via the Holochain DHT.

### J.2 Circle structure and role definitions

### The DNA encodes the nested circle structure central to sociocratic governance:

| ***Circle level***       | ***Domain***                                                                     | ***Composition***                                                 | ***Double-linking***                      | |--------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------| | ***Stewardship circle*** | *Personal regenerative practice, wallet history, local projects*                 | *Individual agents, families, local stewards*                     | *Elects delegate to Community circle*     | | ***Community circle***   | *Local projects, mutual credit, community governance*                            | *Representatives from Stewardship circles*                        | *Double-linked to bioregional circle*     | | ***Bioregional circle*** | *Cross-community coordination, resource allocation, bioregional strategy*        | *Delegates from Community circles*                                | *Double-linked to Prometheus circle*      | | ***Prometheus circle***  | *Constitutional maintenance, protocol evolution, eternity clause interpretation* | *Representatives from bioregional circles + TRBK-elected members* | *Ultimate interpreter; subject to recall* |

### Role definitions within each circle:

| ***Role***                        | ***Responsibilities***                                                  | ***Selection method***                    | ***Term***             | |-----------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------|------------------------| | ***Facilitator***                 | *Guides meetings, ensures consent process, maintains circle focus*      | *Sociocratic election (consent-based)*    | *12 months, renewable* | | ***Secretary***                   | *Maintains records, documents decisions, manages circle artifacts*      | *Sociocratic election*                    | *12 months, renewable* | | ***Delegate (to parent circle)*** | *Represents circle in higher-level governance, brings information down* | *Elected by circle members*               | *12 months, renewable* | | ***Operational roles***           | *Project-specific responsibilities (treasurer, validator, etc.)*        | *Created as needed, sociocratic election* | *Variable*             |

### J.3 Decision processes

### The DNA supports multiple decision-making protocols, selectable by circle governance:

### J.3.1 Consent (Default for all circles)

Consent is the standard decision protocol for all governance matters. A proposal is adopted when no circle member has a reasoned and paramount objection—an objection based on evidence that the proposal would harm the circle's ability to achieve its purpose.

### Process flow:

1.  *Proposal is formulated and published (with minimum 7-day deliberation period)*

2.  *Facilitator calls for consent*

3.  *Members may state: consent, stand aside, or objection*

4.  *Objections are explored and integrated*

5.  *Modified proposal returns to step 2, or if no objections remain, proposal passes*

### Technical implementation:

### rust

### struct ConsentVote {

### proposal_id: Hash,

### member_id: AgentPubKey,

### decision: ConsentDecision, // Consent, StandAside, Objection

### objection_reason: Option\<String\>,

### timestamp: Timestamp,

### signature: Signature

### }

### J.3.2 Consent with weighted reputation

For certain operational decisions, circles may choose to weight member consent by reputation (see Section J.4). A supermajority of weighted consent is required (threshold configurable per circle, default 60%).

### J.3.3 Futarchy (conditional)

For complex, high-stakes decisions, a circle may optionally adopt futarchy: decisions are made by betting on outcomes. This requires:

- *Prediction markets on the DHT for specific decision outcomes*

- *Staking of TRBK or other whitelisted tokens*

- *Post-decision verification via MRV data*

- *Automatic payout based on accuracy*

Futarchy is only available to circles with demonstrated governance maturity (minimum 24 months existence, supermajority approval).

### J.3.4 Constitutional amendments (Article XV)

Constitutional amendments follow the strict process defined in Article XV, including TRBK-only initiation, supermajority voting, and Prometheus circle veto with override provisions. This is hard-coded at the DNA level and cannot be altered by ordinary governance.

### J.4 Reputation algorithms

Reputation is a multidimensional, non-transferable metric that tracks an agent's history of contributions, reliability, and constitutional alignment. It influences governance weight, access to resources, and eligibility for roles.

### J.4.1 Reputation components

| *Component*                | *Weight* | *Data source*                                                  | *Update frequency*      | |----------------------------|----------|----------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------------| | *Contribution Score*       | *40%*    | *REA events (projects participated in, resources contributed)* | *Real-time*             | | *Reliability Score*        | *30%*    | *Commitments respected vs. broken, warrant history*            | *After each commitment* | | *Coherence Score*          | *15%*    | *Aggregated HSI metrics (anonymized)*                          | *Monthly*               | | *Validation Accuracy*      | *10%*    | *Accuracy of MRV validations, oracle performance*              | *Per validation*        | | *Governance Participation* | *5%*     | *Voting history, proposal quality, circle attendance*          | *Per governance event*  |

### J.4.2 Reputation calculation

Reputation is calculated locally by each node and gossiped through the DHT, ensuring consistency without centralization. The formula:

### R_total = (Σ w_i · s_i) / (Σ w_i) · (1 - p_warrants)

### Where:

- *w_i are component weights*

- *s_i are normalized component scores (0-1)*

- *p_warrants is a penalty factor based on active warrants (0-0.5)*

Reputation decay: Reputation slowly decays over time (configurable, default 5% per year) to incentivize continued participation and prevent "resting on laurels."

### J.4.3 Cross-token reputation

The reputation system is token-agnostic but wallet-aware. An agent's history of contributions across multiple token communities (TRBK, bioregional tokens, etc.) is aggregated into a unified reputation profile, accessible with appropriate privacy controls. This enables:

- *Trust to travel across communities*

- *Reduced friction for agents joining new circles*

- *Prevention of Sybil attacks (new agents start with zero reputation)*

### J.5 Warrant handling

Warrants are signed declarations of misbehavior, issued by nodes when they detect constitutional violations, data falsification, or other bad acts. They are the immune system's first line of defense.

### J.5.1 Warrant types

| ***Warrant type***             | ***Description***                                              | ***Issuance threshold***                           | |--------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------| | ***Data integrity violation*** | *Falsified MRV data, invalid transactions*                     | *Single node detection*                            | | ***Constitutional violation*** | *Code or action violating eternity clauses*                    | *Single node detection + Prometheus circle review* | | ***Reputation fraud***         | *Artificially inflating reputation through collusion*          | *Consensus of neighborhood (r/2+1 nodes)*          | | ***Double-send attempt***      | *Attempt to claim same regenerative event for multiple tokens* | *Automatic from neighborhood validation*           |

### J.5.2 Warrant lifecycle

1.  ***Issuance:** Any node may issue a warrant, which is signed and propagated to the neighborhood.*

2.  ***Challenge period:** The accused agent has 7 days to respond, providing evidence or contesting the warrant.*

3.  ***Neighborhood review:** The warrant is reviewed by the neighborhood (random subset of r nodes). If at least r/2+1 nodes validate the warrant, it becomes active.*

4.  ***Penalties:** Active warrants trigger:*

- *Reputation penalty (see Section J.4.2)*

- *Possible slashing of staked tokens (configurable per token)*

- *Temporary or permanent role exclusion (circle vote)*

5.  ***Appeal:** Warrants may be appealed to the next-higher circle (up to Prometheus circle), which can override with supermajority.*

### J.5.3 False warrant penalties

### To prevent abuse, nodes that issue false warrants are themselves subject to penalties:

- *Reputation loss for the issuing node*

- *Slashing of staked TRBK (if applicable)*

- *Potential exclusion from validation roles*

### J.6 Integration with other DNAs

| ***DNA***        | ***Integration point***                                                                       | |------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------| | *REA/Valueflows* | *Reputation updates based on completed commitments; warrants linked to disputed transactions* | | *MRV*            | *Validation accuracy tracked; warrants for data falsification*                                | | *TRBK*           | *Governance weight influenced by reputation; staking and slashing mechanisms*                 | | *Holo Hosting*   | *Node uptime and reliability influence reputation; warrants for service failures*             | | *Decision Log*   | *All governance decisions recorded for audit and future training*                             |

### J.7 Privacy and transparency

The Governance & Reputation DNA balances radical transparency (all decisions are auditable) with privacy (individual voting choices may be shielded via zero-knowledge proofs where appropriate).

| ***Data type***         | ***Visibility***                                                | ***Privacy mechanism***                  | |-------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------| | ***Final decisions***   | *Public on DHT*                                                 | *None needed*                            | | ***Individual votes***  | *Circle-configurable (public, revealed after vote, or private)* | *ZK-proofs for tally verification*       | | ***Reputation scores*** | *Public aggregate; component details private*                   | *Merkle proofs for selective disclosure* | | ***Warrants***          | *Public*                                                        | *None needed*                            |

Detailed technical specifications, including complete data structures, validation rules, and API endpoints, are maintained in the separate technical documentation package.

## Appendix K: Planetary boundaries integration

### K.1 Overview

The h

- eart
- h Prometheus protocol integrates the Planetary Boundaries framework as a foundational layer for ecological integrity assessment. This appendix specifies the technical implementation of planetary boundary monitoring, threshold calculations, and the derivation of the Planetary Health Index (PHI) used throughout the ecosystem for risk assessment and regenerative brake activation.

The framework follows the 2023 revision of the Planetary Boundaries and aligns with the latest scientific consensus from the Stockholm Resilience Centre, the Potsdam Institute for climate impact research, and the Planetary boundaries science (PBScience) Lab.

### K.2 The nine planetary boundaries: Indicators and data sources

### K.3 Planetary Health Index (PHI) algorithm

The Planetary Health Index (PHI) is a composite metric that synthesizes the state of all nine planetary boundaries into a single normalized score ranging from 0 to 1, where 1 represents full alignment with the safe operating space and 0 represents catastrophic transgression. PHI serves as a critical input to the Minsky-Keen Ravel software (see Appendix C) and as a key performance indicator for bioregional assessments, project evaluation, and systemic risk management throughout the h

- eart
- h ecosystem.

### K.3.1 Calculation methodology

### The PHI algorithm follows a three-step process:

### Step 1: Boundary-specific normalization

For boundaries with qualitative assessments (e.g., novel entities), scores are determined annually by the ecological oracle network based on peer-reviewed scientific consensus, using a discrete scale (0.0, 0.25, 0.5, 0.75, or 1.0).

For each planetary boundary i, a normalized score s_i is calculated based on the position of the current control variable value v_i relative to scientifically established thresholds. The score indicates the boundary's health status:

- *s_i = 1.0 → Safely within the boundary (green zone)*

- *s_i = 0.0 → Boundary exceeded (red zone)*

- *0.0 \< s_i \< 1.0 → Zone of increasing risk (yellow zone)*

### Two formulas are applied depending on the direction of the threat:

**Formula A: For boundaries where increasing values indicate greater risk** (Applies to: climate change, biogeochemical flows, novel entities, atmospheric aerosol loading)

| ***Condition***  | ***Normalized score (sᵢ)***        | |------------------|------------------------------------| | *vᵢ ≤ tₗ*        | *sᵢ = 1.0*                         | | *tₗ \< vᵢ \< tₕ* | *sᵢ = 1.0 – (vᵢ – tₗ) / (tₕ – tₗ)* | | *vᵢ ≥ tₕ*        | *sᵢ = 0.0*                         |

**Formula B: For boundaries where decreasing values indicate greater risk** (Applies to: biosphere integrity, land-system change, freshwater use, ocean acidification, stratospheric ozone)

| ***Condition***  | ***Normalized score (sᵢ)***        | |------------------|------------------------------------| | *vᵢ ≥ tₕ*        | *sᵢ = 1.0*                         | | *tₗ \< vᵢ \< tₕ* | *sᵢ = 1.0 – (tₕ – vᵢ) / (tₕ – tₗ)* | | *vᵢ ≤ tₗ*        | *sᵢ = 0.0*                         |

### Where:

- *vᵢ = current value of the control variable*

- *tₗ = lower threshold (where the zone of increasing risk begins, or where the boundary is considered transgressed for Formula B)*

- *tₕ = upper threshold (where the boundary is considered transgressed for Formula A, or where the zone of increasing risk begins for Formula B)*

### Step 2: Weighting and aggregation

Once each boundary has a normalized score sᵢ, the PHI is calculated using a weighted geometric mean. This method reflects the interconnected and non-substitutable nature of Earth system processes: a catastrophic failure in one boundary cannot be compensated by success in others.

### PHI = (∏\_{i=1}^{9} s_i^{w_i})^{1/Σ w_i}

### The weights wᵢ are scientifically derived based on:

- *The boundary's role in Earth system stability (core regulating processes weighted higher)*

- *Current transgression severity*

- *Telecoupling strength (how strongly the boundary influences others)*

The current weight set, derived from expert consultation and published in the Planetary health check 2025, is:

| ***Planetary boundary***          | ***Weight*** | ***Scientific rationale***                                                   | |-----------------------------------|--------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------| | ***Climate change***              | *1.2*        | *Primary Earth system regulator; affects all other boundaries*               | | ***Biosphere integrity***         | *1.2*        | *Foundational for ecosystem services; irreversible once lost*                | | ***Biogeochemical flows***        | *1.0*        | *Critical for food production and water quality; regional to global impacts* | | ***Land system change***          | *1.0*        | *Direct driver of habitat loss and carbon emissions*                         | | ***Freshwater use***              | *0.9*        | *Essential for human and ecosystem health; local to regional*                | | ***Ocean acidification***         | *0.8*        | *Direct threat to marine food webs; closely coupled with climate*            | | ***Stratospheric ozone***         | *0.7*        | *Successfully managed; continued monitoring essential*                       | | ***Atmospheric aerosol loading*** | *0.6*        | *Regional impacts; high uncertainty in thresholds*                           | | ***Novel entities***              | *0.6*        | *Emerging concern; qualitative assessment currently required*                |

**Why a geometric mean?** The geometric mean ensures that if any single boundary scores zero (i.e., is catastrophically transgressed), the entire PHI becomes zero. This mathematically encodes the scientific reality that Earth's systems are deeply interconnected—failure in one can trigger cascading failures across others.

### Step 3: Spatial and temporal aggregation

### For bioregional assessments, PHI can be calculated at multiple scales:

| ***Scale***       | ***Data sources***                                                                                                                             | ***Application***                                                  | |-------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------| | *Global PHI*      | *Global mean values from scientific databases (e.g., NOAA, IPCC, FAO)*                                                                         | *Planetary health monitoring; high-level reporting*                | | *Bioregional PHI* | *Downscaled using high-resolution datasets (e.g., 5 km FLUXCOM X BASE for biosphere integrity, WaterGAP for freshwater) and local MRV sensors* | *Project evaluation; bioregional governance; investment decisions* | | *Temporal PHI*    | *Calculated as a moving average (typically 3- to 5-year window) of global or bioregional PHI*                                                  | *Trend analysis; early warning; policy effectiveness*              |

### The Ravel software continuously monitors two critical signals:

- ***Absolute PHI value** – Determines current systemic health and triggers graduated responses when falling below thresholds.*

- ***Rate of change (ΔPHI/Δt)** – Provides early warning of deteriorating trends before absolute thresholds are crossed.*

A sustained decline in PHI, even while absolute values remain above critical thresholds, activates the yellow regenerative brake—proactive intervention to reverse negative trends before they become irreversible.

### K.3.2 PHI thresholds and analysis

The PHI score provides an intuitive yet scientifically robust framework for decision making:

| ***PHI Range*** | ***Status*** | ***Systemic response***                                              | |-----------------|--------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------| | *1.0*           | *Optimal*    | *All boundaries respected; system in regenerative state*             | | *0.8 – 0.99*    | *Safe*       | *Some boundaries approached; enhanced monitoring recommended*        | | *0.5 – 0.79*    | *Caution*    | *Multiple boundaries in increasing risk zone; prepare interventions* | | *0.2 – 0.49*    | *Critical*   | *Boundaries transgressed; emergency measures required*               | | *\< 0.2*        | *Collapse*   | *Catastrophic failure; system-wide regeneration imperative*          |

### K.3.3 Integration with the three-plane architecture

| ***Plane***    | ***PHI Integration***                                                                                                                                                    | |----------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------| | *Experiential* | *PHI is visualized in regeneration dashboards, allowing communities and investors to track ecosystem health at global and bioregional scales.*                           | | *Cognitive*    | *Specialist agents (ReFi/Minsky agent, Ecological design agent) use PHI as a key constraint in business plan generation, risk assessment, and scenario modeling.*        | | *Operational*  | *PHI is hashed to the DHT, recorded in the Decision Log DNA, and used by the Ravel Software to trigger the regenerative brake when PHI falls below critical thresholds.* |

### K.4 Threshold calculation and calibration

The planetary boundary thresholds used in the h

- eart
- h protocol are continuously calibrated using multiple scientific methodologies:

| *Methodology*                         | *Application*                                                                                                                                                                        | *Source*                                      | |---------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------| | ***ROC/AUC analysis***                | *Threshold optimization for locally variable boundaries (biosphere integrity, freshwater, land use) using Receiver Operating Characteristic curves and Area Under the Curve metrics* | *Ben Uri et al., EGU 2025*                    | | ***Earth system models (ESMs)***      | *Climate sensitivity, ocean acidification, and aerosol impacts modeled using CMIP6 and Earth system models*                                                                          | *IPCC AR6, Potsdam Institute*                 | | ***Paleo ecological reconstruction*** | *Holocene baseline determination for green water, biosphere integrity, and land system change*                                                                                       | *Vostok ice cores, GRIP, paleo data archives* | | ***Expert elicitation***              | *Novel entities and boundaries with high uncertainty*                                                                                                                                | *PBScience Lab, Planetary Guardians*          |

Thresholds are updated annually following the release of the Planetary Health Check report and any major scientific revisions (e.g., the 2023 framework update).

### K.5 Data integration and quality assurance

All planetary boundary data integrated into the h

- eart
- h ecosystem undergoes rigorous quality assurance:

| ***Quality measure***               | ***Description***                                                                                                                                | |-------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------| | ***Multi-source cross validation*** | *Each control variable is sourced from at least two independent providers*                                                                       | | ***Provenance tracking***           | *All data transformations are recorded in the Decision Log DNA*                                                                                  | | ***Uncertainty quantification***    | *Confidence intervals are propagated through PHI calculations*                                                                                   | | ***Temporal consistency***          | *Time series are gap-filled using established interpolation methods (linear interpolation for short gaps, climatological means for longer gaps)* |

### K.6 Limitations and research frontiers

The current PHI implementation acknowledges several limitations that guide ongoing research and development:

| ***Limitation***                    | ***Description***                                                          | ***Mitigation strategy***                                                                          | |-------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------| | ***Spatial heterogeneity***         | *Global mean values may mask critical regional transgressions*             | *Bioregional downscaling using high-resolution datasets (e.g., European sub-national assessments)* | | ***Temporal lag***                  | *Some datasets (e.g., extinction rates) have significant reporting delays* | *Real-time sensor integration; predictive modeling using AI*                                       | | ***Novel entities quantification*** | *Lack of quantitative thresholds requires qualitative assessment*          | *Annual expert assessment; research into proxy indicators*                                         | | ***Interaction effects***           | *Current PHI aggregation assumes partial independence*                     | *Ongoing research into fully coupled Earth system models*                                          |

The protocol is designed to incorporate scientific advances as they emerge, particularly in:

- *High-resolution downscaling of planetary boundaries*

- *Integration of ocean processes into the framework*

- *AI-enhanced predictive modeling of boundary transgressions*

- *Refinement of interaction weights through empirical observation*

Detailed technical specifications, including API endpoints for real-time data access, data processing pipelines, and validation scripts, are maintained in Appendix L and the separate technical documentation package.

## Appendix L: Integration zome API documentation

### L.1 Overview

The Integration Zome is the primary gateway for external systems to interact with the h

- eart
- h Prometheus ecosystem. It provides a secure, authenticated interface for data ingestion, query execution, and cross-chain interoperability while maintaining strict constitutional enforcement via the syntropic sovereignty header. This appendix specifies the API architecture, endpoint definitions, authentication mechanisms, rate limiting policies, and external system connectors.

The Integration Zome is designed to be protocol-agnostic, supporting multiple API paradigms to accommodate diverse integration scenarios:

| ***Protocol*** | ***Use case***                                                                      | ***Advantages***                                                      | |----------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------| | ***REST***     | *Simple data retrieval, webhook integrations, legacy system connectivity*           | *Universal compatibility, stateless, easy to cache*                   | | ***GraphQL***  | *Complex queries, real-time dashboards, front-end applications*                     | *Efficient data fetching, strong typing, subscription support*        | | ***gRPC***     | *High-throughput data exchange, inter-service communication, real-time sensor data* | *Bi-directional streaming, high performance, built-in authentication* |

All API endpoints are subject to the syntropic sovereignty header validation, ensuring that every request and response respects the constitutional principles of non-commodification of life, agent sovereignty, and the spiral of abundance.

### L.2 Authentication and authorization

All API requests must be authenticated and authorized. The Integration Zome supports multiple authentication methods, each appropriate for different use cases and trust levels.

### L.2.1 Authentication methods

| ***Method***                     | ***Description***                                                       | ***Use case***                                                           | |----------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------| | ***API key***                    | *Simple token-based authentication for low-risk read operations*        | *Public data access, dashboard queries, non-sensitive MRV data*          | | ***JWT (JSON Web Token)***       | *Time-limited, signed tokens containing agent identity and permissions* | *User-authenticated requests, governance participation, token transfers* | | ***Holochain Agent signature***  | *Cryptographic signature using agent's private key, verified via DPKI*  | *High-security operations, constitutional amendments, warrant issuance*  | | ***OAuth 2.0 / OpenID connect*** | *Delegated authentication via trusted identity providers*               | *Integration with external platforms, enterprise SSO*                    |

### L.2.2 Authorization levels

| ***Level***               | ***Permissions***                                                  | ***Required authentication***                | |---------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------| | ***Public***              | *Read-only access to non-sensitive aggregated data*                | *API Key (optional)*                         | | ***Authenticated agent*** | *Read/write access for agent's own data, governance participation* | *JWT or Holochain signature*                 | | ***Validator***           | *Validation node operations, warrant issuance*                     | *Holochain signature + staked TRBK*          | | ***Circle delegate***     | *Circle governance actions, proposal submission*                   | *JWT + role verification via Governance DNA* | | ***Prometheus circle***   | *Constitutional interpretation, veto authority*                    | *Multi-signature (≥2/3 of circle)*           |

### L.2.3 API key management

### API keys are issued through the Governance DNA and can be scoped to:

- *Specific IP ranges*

- *Specific endpoints*

- *Rate limit tiers*

- *Expiration dates*

Keys are hashed and stored on the DHT; the plaintext key is only shown once at creation. For security, keys should be rotated periodically.
